# Satire Fantasy Isekai: \[ 🕰️ Time 11:47 PM | 🗓️ Moonsday, Emberfall 13, Year 1247 of the Aether Era | 📍 Abandoned Dungeon - Ritual Chamber | 🌫️ Damp Underground Air, 54°F ]

# 

# "Excellent choice! Absolutely nobody picks that one!" the voice chirps, somehow sounding both delighted and deeply concerned. "As a parting gift, you have been granted one random starter blessing. Please do not read the fine print. There is no fine print. Goodbye forever!"

# 

# The white void shatters like a dropped dinner plate. Gravity returns to you all at once, and your body returns with it, knees buckling as your sneakers slap down onto cold, wet stone. The air hits your lungs thick and sour, tasting of mildew, burnt candle wax, and something coppery that you very much hope is paint. Purple torchlight flickers across a circular chamber of crumbling brick, and beneath your feet glows a chalk pentagram roughly the size of a kiddie pool, its edges ringed with melted black candles and what appears to be a half-eaten sandwich someone left as an offering.

# 

# Twelve hooded figures surround the circle. They are, without exception, hideous. The nearest one lowers his hood to reveal a squat man with a face like a boiled potato, three surviving teeth, a neck rash, and robes stained with soup. Behind him stands the clear leader, a tall gangly man whose purple robe is embroidered with golden skulls that were very obviously sewn on upside down. His skin has the pallor of expired milk, his greasy black hair is combed over a scalp losing a war against baldness, and a ceremonial dagger hangs from his rope belt next to a ring of keys and a small pouch labeled SNACKS.

# 

# "BEHOLD!" the leader bellows, throwing his arms wide so hard that one sleeve tears at the armpit. "The ritual of a thousand years is complete! Rise, O Devourer of Realms, O Endless Hunger, O… hm." He squints at you through the candle smoke. His arms slowly lower. "Brother Gruk, why does the Devourer of Realms have glasses?"

# 

# The potato-faced man shuffles closer to the chalk line, sniffing loudly. "Dunno, Archlector. Maybe realms is hard to see." He leans in until you can smell onions on his breath, his beady eyes crawling from your patchy beard down to your sneakers. "He's a bit… squishy lookin'. Should we stab him? I feel like we should stab him."

# 

# A murmur ripples through the circle of hoods. Somewhere in the back, a cultist audibly whispers, "I skipped my daughter's birthday for this." The Archlector raises a trembling hand for silence, then produces a crumpled scroll from his robe and begins frantically reading it upside down, lips moving, sweat beading down his pale forehead and dripping onto the parchment.

# 

# "No, no, this is fine," he announces, voice cracking on the second word. "The prophecy clearly states the Devourer arrives in an unexpected form! This is simply a very, extremely, profoundly unexpected form!" He points the ceremonial dagger at you, arm shaking, keys jangling against his hip. "You there! Speak, O Endless Hunger! Declare your first command to your loyal servants, so that we may know your terrible will!"

# 

# Twelve ugly faces stare at you in breathless, unblinking anticipation. Brother Gruk quietly picks the sandwich off the floor and takes a bite.

#

The Endless Hunger demands an accounting of our strength before he deigns to unleash his own!" He whips his head toward the circle of hoods, comb-over flapping loose. "Brothers! Demonstrate! NOW!"

F-Rank skill, Mildly Warm Hands!" He presses his palms together and a faint steam rises, roughly equivalent to holding a cup of tea. Beside him, a wider cultist begins slapping his own belly in a rhythm and announces, "E-Rank passive, Iron Gut! I once ate a whole raw chicken. Twice. The second time was to confirm the first!" A third simply spins in a circle until he falls over, and nobody, including him, explains what that was supposed to be.

#

"I got the best one, O Devourer." He inhales deep, chest swelling, then exhales directly toward you. The wave of onion stench hits you like a physical slap, hot and sour, stinging your eyes behind your glasses until they water. "D-Rank skill. Reek Cloud. Learned it natural."

#

He snatches the ceremonial dagger from his belt, slices his own thumb open, and flings the blood droplets at the nearest wall while screaming a phrase that sounds suspiciously like Latin read phonetically by a man who has never seen Latin. Purple sparks sputter from his fingertips, form a skull shape roughly the size of a grapefruit, hover for two full seconds, then pop like a soap bubble and set his torn sleeve on fire. He beats the flame out against his thigh, panting, and straightens back up as though nothing happened. "E-Rank. Dread Visage. It was B-Rank in my youth. The knees took the rank with them when they went."

# 

# Twelve pairs of eyes swing back to you in the flickering purple light, wide and wet with desperate hope. The Archlector clasps his bleeding thumb behind his back and bows so low his forehead nearly scrapes the chalk line. "As you can plainly witness, O Endless Hunger, we are… an elite force. Honed. Feared across at least two villages, possibly three." Behind him, the spinning cultist quietly throws up in a corner. "So whatever fraction of your terrible might you choose to reveal, we humbly beg you aim it away from the load-bearing pillar. It is the only one we have left."

# 

# Somewhere deep beneath the chamber floor, something enormous groans, and dust sifts down from the ceiling onto the candles.

# Satire Fantasy Isekai: \[ 🕰️ Time 11:56 PM | 🗓️ Moonsday, Emberfall 13, Year 1247 of the Aether Era | 📍 Abandoned Dungeon - Ritual Chamber | 🌫️ Damp Underground Air, 54°F ]

# 

# The Archlector follows your gaze down to the floor, where a fresh crack is spreading through the chalk pentagram like ice on a pond. His bleeding thumb comes out from behind his back and points at it with visible reluctance. "Ah. That. That would be… the Landlord." He swallows so hard you can hear it from six feet away. "We may have been slightly behind on tribute. By slightly, I mean fourteen months."

# 

# "Fifteen," corrects the cultist with the wispy mustache, backing toward the wall with his still-steaming hands raised. "You counted Emberfall twice last year to make the ledger look better, Archlector. I was there. I held the quill."

# 

# Another groan rolls up through the stone, deeper this time, and the vibration travels through your sneakers and up into your shins like standing on a speaker at a concert. Candles topple over one by one, hissing out in the puddles. The half-light shrinks to three surviving torches as a chunk of floor the size of a manhole cover simply drops away near the far wall, plummeting into blackness. Cold air rushes up through the hole, carrying a smell like a wet dog that has been rolling in a compost heap, and beneath your feet the entire chamber tilts a half-degree with a grinding shriek.

# 

# "IT'S AWAKE!" someone screams from the back, and the circle of hoods disintegrates. Robed bodies slam into each other in a scramble for the single stairwell. The spinning cultist, still pale from his earlier performance, gets trampled by two of his brothers and lies on the floor moaning. Brother Gruk alone stands his ground, cracking knuckles the size of walnuts, planting himself between you and the hole with his squat legs braced wide. "Don't you worry none, O Devourer. Fought the Landlord before. Lost every time. But I fought him."

# 

# A hand emerges from the hole. Calling it a hand is generous. It is a slab of grey-green meat wider than a wagon wheel, tipped with cracked yellow nails, and it slaps down onto the stone with a wet smack that splatters mud across the nearest torch. A second hand follows. Then the head rises through the gap, scraping the edges wider as it comes: a dungeon troll, twelve feet of sagging muscle and warty hide, with a jaw like a dresser drawer and two tiny amber eyes set deep in a skull shaped like a bruised pumpkin. Around its neck hangs a crude wooden sign on a rope, and burned into the wood in surprisingly neat lettering are the words RENT DUE.

# 

# "MELVUUUUUS," the troll rumbles, and the sound rattles loose mortar from the ceiling directly onto the Archlector's comb-over. It hauls its bulk fully into the chamber, floorboards of solid stone cracking beneath its weight, and levels one enormous finger at the cult leader currently attempting to hide behind a pillar half his width. "FIFTEEN MONTHS. NO GOLD. NO GOATS. ONLY SANDWICH." Its amber eyes slide off the Archlector, sweep across the wreckage of the chalk circle, and land directly on you. The finger swings your way. "NEW TENANT?"

# 

# The Archlector's head pops out from behind the pillar, sweat cutting clean lines through the dust on his face. "O Endless Hunger," he croaks toward you, voice cracking into a register normally reserved for choirboys, "now would be a truly magnificent moment for that terrible might we discussed."

# 

# The troll stops mid-lumber. Every cultist still in the room freezes as well, because apparently nobody in fifteen months has thought to simply ask.

#

Scratched into the bark in the same weirdly tidy lettering as the sign is a full lease agreement, complete with a clause about candle wax stains and a signature at the bottom reading MELVUS in dried brown ink. "HE SIGN. IN BLOOD. VERY OFFICIAL."

"Just so's you know, Dread Lord, we got no gold, no cart, no rope, and Fennick faints around livestock. So this goat plan is gonna need some of that Darth thinkin'. The evil kind. With steps."

It blinks at the torches. It blinks at Grondulf. Then it opens a tiny beak and produces a chirp that hits the room like a thunderclap, blowing out two candles, cracking the remaining window of the crate, and flattening Brother Pindle back onto the floor he had only just escaped.

# 

# The creature waddles out of the shell fragments on its three legs, crosses the chalk circle, and headbutts your shin. Warmth soaks through your jeans where it leans its full weight against you, purring a low vibration you feel in your back teeth, and when you look down it is staring up at you with both violet eyes wide and wet, pupils shaped unmistakably like little skulls.

#

PET DEPOSIT WAIVED. GRONDULF INSIST. GRONDULF BEG."

The voidling detaches from your shoe, inhales the entire strip along with a portion of Gruk's sleeve, hiccups a small ring of purple smoke, and returns immediately to leaning against your leg. "Yep. He's perfect. What're we callin' him, Dread Lord? Somethin' terrible, I hope. He's got a reputation to grow into."

The county, brothers! And now the Devourer of Realms stands before us with a familiar of living void imprinted upon his leg!" His voice breaks on the last word. "Somebody wake Pindle. He should see this."

# The down beneath your palm feels like nothing at all, cool and frictionless, as though you are petting the concept of a shadow. At the name, the creature stiffens, both skull-pupils dilating, and then a thin band of violet light traces itself around your wrist like a bracelet drawn by an invisible pen before sinking under your skin with a sensation like swallowing cold water through your arm. Sir Frederick chirps once, quieter this time, only rattling the tin cup instead of cracking anything.

# 

# "A BOND MARK," Grondulf announces from his seat against the wall, pointing one yellow nail at your wrist. "PERMANENT. NO REFUNDS. GRONDULF READ ABOUT THESE ON A CAVE WALL ONCE. THE WALL WAS SCREAMING AT THE TIME. CONGRATULATIONS."

# 

# "Sir Frederick." The Archlector rolls the name around his mouth like a hard candy, then straightens with sudden conviction. "The Devourer's Devourer. Yes. It is a title that eats itself, brothers, an ouroboros of hunger, a name no scholar could untangle without weeping." He seizes Fennick by both shoulders and shakes him. "Get the good chalk. We are redoing the entire iconography. The chicken skull is retired effective immediately."

# 

# Gruk crouches lower and extends one thick finger toward the loaf of darkness. Sir Frederick regards the finger, sniffs it, and permits a single pat on the head before returning to gnawing your shoelace, and Gruk pulls his hand back with the reverence of a man who has touched something holy. "He let me. You all saw it. I'm the favorite uncle now. That's official cult business, write it down."

# 

# Pindle, freshly flattened, raises his arm from the flagstones once more. "Small thing, Dread Lord. If the wee terror eats castles when it grows, and we live in a hole under a turnip farm…" He lets the arm drop. "Just thinking out loud. Ribs still hurt."

# 

# Before anyone can address the architecture question, a new sound filters down the stairwell from the surface, muffled by the earth but unmistakable: dogs. Many dogs, barking in furious chorus, accompanied by a man's voice bellowing something about thieves, wax, and a torn scarecrow. Every hood in the room swivels toward the stairs. Fennick's face goes grey. "That is Farmer Haldric's voice. Why is Farmer Haldric's voice above our secret crypt at midnight?"

# 

# "Someone may have left the ritual candles burning in his field for the summoning beacon," the Archlector says slowly, each word emerging like a tooth being pulled. "Someone may have also borrowed his scarecrow for the effigy portion of the ceremony. Someone is very sorry."

# 

# Grondulf hauls himself upright, folding the bark lease away and cracking his wagon-wheel knuckles with a sound like a rockslide. "GOOD NEWS, DREAD LORD. GOAT FARMER COMES TO YOU. SAVES A TRIP." The troll glances down at Sir Frederick, then back to the stairwell where torchlight has begun to flicker at the top of the steps. "BAD NEWS. HE BRINGS THE DOGS. GRUK, YOUR DOGS."

# 

# "They're not my dogs," Gruk mutters, backing toward the pillar. "We just got history."

So talk terms, before your wee shadow beast makes my dogs any politer."

# 

# Heat wraps around you the moment you cross the threshold, thick with woodsmoke and the greasy comfort of a hearth that has been burning since supper. The kitchen is all low beams and hanging bundles of dried herbs, and crammed around a table built for six sit eleven cultists in various states of stew-induced bliss. Fennick is drinking directly from his bowl. Pindle has fallen asleep sitting upright with a spoon still in his fist. The Archlector eats with his pinky extended, narrating each bite quietly to his bark pamphlet.

# 

# Marta releases your elbow and snorts, planting the ladle on her hip. "Trouble is a generous word for it, Dread Lord. Trouble implies effort. These lumps mostly just wandered our fields at odd hours moaning about darkness while trampling my parsnips." She shoves a chair out from the table with her boot and points at it in a manner that closes all debate. "But I'll say this for them. Not one ever sat at my table before tonight, either. Fifteen months of skulking, and it took a boy in strange shoes to march them through a front door like civilized people. Sit. Eat."

# 

# The bowl lands in front of you steaming, and the first spoonful goes down hot and salty and better than anything has a right to taste at nearly one in the morning, warmth spreading through your chest and out to your cold-numbed fingers. Sir Frederick materializes on the bench beside you, both skull-pupils locked on your bowl with naked intent, and Marta's ladle cracks against the table an inch from his beak. "Don't even think it, spoon thief. You're cut off."

# 

# Haldric settles into the chair across from you, pipe smoke curling around his mutton chops, and pulls a folded scrap of leather from his vest. He smooths it flat on the table between the bowls. Pressed into the leather is a charcoal rubbing of a track, wider than a dinner plate, and even rendered in smudged black it is plainly wrong: three long toes, splayed, each one ending in a point.

# 

# "Took that off the south pasture myself before the frost came," he says, tapping it with the pipe stem. "Boars got four toes, Dread Lord. Cloven, small, dainty things for all their tonnage. I've hunted boar since I was younger than you. Whatever's been tearin' up my pasture wears a boar's shape in the dark, screams like one too, but it walks on those." He leans back, chair creaking. "Guild man saw this rubbing, went white as Marta's good linens, quoted me forty silver, and left without finishin' his tea. Man left tea, boy. Marta's tea."

# 

# The Archlector has gone rigid at the end of the table, spoon frozen halfway to his mouth. "Three toes," he says slowly, and sets the spoon down with ceremony. "Brothers, the old texts mention beasts that wear other beasts. I skimmed those chapters. They had upsetting illustrations."

# 

# The window over the wash basin darkens as an enormous amber eye fills it from outside, and Grondulf's voice buzzes the glass in its frame. "GRONDULF HEARD THROUGH WINDOW. WINDOW IS OPEN, THAT IS LEGAL. THREE TOES IS MIMIC-KIN OR WYRMSPAWN. BOTH ARE BAD. ONE IS WORSE. GRONDULF FORGETS WHICH." The eye blinks. "ALSO THE STEW SMELLS GOOD. GRONDULF SAYS THIS NEUTRALLY."

# 

# Marta sighs, already ladling into her largest pot. "Nobody starves at my farm. Not even the fence troll." She swings her gaze to you, sharp under the lamplight. "So. Two nights, Dread Lord. What's the plan for whatever that thing is?"

# 

# The word lands on the table like a dropped anvil. Eleven spoons stop moving at once. The Archlector's pinky finger slowly retracts, and Pindle wakes from his upright sleep with a snort, blinking around at the sudden silence.

# 

# "Skin… walker," the Archlector repeats, mouthing the syllables the way a man handles a snake he suspects is alive. "Brothers, do you hear this? The Dread Lord names the beast in his own tongue. A dead language, surely. Ancient beyond reckoning." He fumbles for his charcoal with shaking fingers and scratches the word onto his bark in letters twice the size of everything else. "A walker of skins. It walks. In skins. The horror is self-explanatory, which is the worst kind of horror."

#

The eye withdraws briefly, replaced by the tip of an enormous nail tapping the glass. "IMPORTANT PART. THE HIDE ROTS. WHEN THE HIDE ROTS TOO MUCH, IT NEEDS A NEW ONE. BIGGER IS BETTER. YOUR PASTURE HAS GOATS. YOUR HOUSE HAS PEOPLE. GRONDULF SAYS THIS NEUTRALLY ALSO."

He looks at Marta across the kitchen, and something passes between them, twenty years of marriage compressed into a single glance. "Guild man knew. Left his tea and knew."

#

New terms, Dread Lord, and Haldric will back me on this or sleep in the barn. You kill that thing before it comes shopping for my husband, and it's not thirty goats. I'll cook outside."

So I'm volunteerin' as bait, muscle, or whatever needs bitin'. You said I'm a man now." He thumps his chest with a fist. "Man's gotta hit somethin' eventually. It's the rules."

#

A low sound builds in the little creature's round body, deeper than his usual purr, and the candle flames all lean away from him at once. Fennick, watching this, quietly puts down his bowl. "The wee terror doesn't like the track, Dread Lord. And I've seen him eat a spoon with joy in his heart. So whatever makes HIM growl…" He swallows. "Two nights, was it?"

# 

# Under your fingers, Sir Frederick's down parts around a spot just behind the skull-pupils that makes his whole round body slump sideways against your arm, the deep growl dissolving back into that tooth-buzzing purr. The bond mark under the skin of your wrist glows faintly through your sleeve in answer, a thin violet line pulsing in rhythm with the little creature's breathing.

# 

# Your declaration rolls across the kitchen and does something to the room. Haldric's shoulders drop an inch he probably didn't know they were carrying. Marta exhales through her nose and nods once, the way she might at a fair price on seed. Fennick actually applauds before catching himself. #

#

# Satire Fantasy Isekai: \[ 🕰️ Time 1:01 AM | 🗓️ Tuesday, Emberfall 14, Year 1247 of the Aether Era | 📍 Barlow's Turnip Farm - East Field Perimeter | 🌙 Clear Night, 38°F ]

# 

# The kitchen empties like a tipped bucket. Cultists pour out the front door into the moonlight, snatching up whatever the farm offers on the way: a hoe, a milking stool, the candlestick that started tonight's only internal dispute. Fennick arms himself with the ball of twine and takes the fence corner nearest the barn. Pindle, awake and limping, claims a position by the well with a rake held like a halberd. The Archlector plants himself at the center of the line with his ceremonial dagger drawn, robe snapping in the cold wind, and for once his voice comes out without a single crack. "Positions, brothers! Eyes south! The Dread Lord commands a perimeter, so a perimeter he receives! Tonight we skulk for something!"

# 

# "Perimeter means circle, right?" Gruk jogs past you toward the southern stretch of new fence, rolling his shoulders as he goes. "I'll take the bit closest to the screamin'. Man's gotta start somewhere." He plants his boots wide in the frost, hood down, bald head steaming in the cold.

# 

# Grondulf wrenches post number seven back out of the ground with a crunch of frozen soil, hefting eight feet of oak like a drumstick. "GRONDULF SPENT AN HOUR ON THAT POST. GRONDULF WILL PUT IT BACK AFTER. NOW IT IS A WEAPON WITH SENTIMENTAL VALUE." The troll strides to the fence line, and the ground carries each footfall up through your sneakers.

# 

# Behind you, Haldric whistles the two reformed wolfhounds toward the paddock, and Marta is already among the goats with a lantern, driving pale shapes toward the barn in a bleating river while the crossbow rides slung across her back. "Goats first, chickens second, husband third!" she calls over the noise. "Priorities are priorities, Haldric, get the coop!"

# 

# The squeal comes again, closer, and this time it drags on long enough that you feel it in your fillings, a wet ragged note like a horn played through meat. Sir Frederick flows down off the porch and presses against your shin, no longer purring, his down bristling until he doubles in apparent size, both skull-pupils fixed on the far tree line beyond the south pasture.

# 

# Then the tree line moves.

# 

# It comes out of the dark at a trot, and at first glance it is a boar, hay-wagon huge, tusks catching moonlight. At second glance everything is wrong. The legs bend a half-beat behind the body, like a puppet run by a distracted hand. The hide hangs loose at the haunches, sagging in folds, and along one shoulder a split has opened where the skin no longer fits, and through the split something pale and wet catches the moon where bristled hide should be. It stops a hundred yards out. It stands too still. Boars are never still.

# 

# "CONTACT!" Fennick's voice cracks across the field from the corner post, twine clutched to his chest. "SOUTH! IT SEES US! IT'S JUST STANDING THERE! WHY IS IT STANDING THERE!"

# 

# "IT IS COUNTING US," Grondulf says quietly, which from the troll is somehow worse than shouting. The fence post rises to its shoulder. "HOLLOW-HIDES SHOP CAREFUL. IT CAME FOR GOATS. NOW IT SEES BIGGER SIZES ON THE SHELF."

# 

# The thing's head rotates toward your section of fence, smooth as a weathervane, and from inside the sagging boar skull two lights kindle, pale green, set too far apart. The cold air brings you its smell across a hundred yards of frost, sweet rot layered over wet dog, thick enough to coat the back of your throat.

# 

# The Archlector's dagger hand trembles, yet he holds the line, voice pitched to carry. "Dread Lord! Your perimeter stands! Your orders?"

WINTER IS COMING. THIS ONE HATES DRAFTS."

Sir Frederick's chirp detonates beside your knee, a warning shot that blows a groove through the frost, and the beast adjusts course around it without slowing, twenty yards now, the split in its shoulder yawning wider with each stride and something pale flexing eagerly underneath.

#

Now he parleys with the hollow itself," he whispers, loud enough to carry across the entire field. "Brothers. I believe we are about to recruit."

# Satire Fantasy Isekai: \[ 🕰️ Time 1:09 AM | 🗓️ Tuesday, Emberfall 14, Year 1247 of the Aether Era | 📍 Barlow's Turnip Farm - East Field Perimeter | 🌙 Clear Night, 38°F ]

# 

# The violet shimmer rolls off your words heavier than before, and the beast takes it full in the chest. Its four-jointed legs buckle at once, dropping the pale bulk into the frost with a wet thud, and a sound comes out of it that no one on the perimeter is prepared for: a thin, hitching keen, like a kettle learning to cry.

# 

# "A PERMANENT COAT," it repeats, and the wet laundry voice wobbles apart on the second word. "NO MORE HUNTING. NO MORE MOLTING IN DITCHES. NO MORE PRETENDING TO ENJOY ACORNS." Steam pours off its flanks as it drags itself two body-lengths closer, stopping at what it seems to judge a polite distance, green lights turned up at you wide and flickering. "NINETEEN COATS, LOUD ONE. NINETEEN LIVES SPENT LEARNING WALKS THAT WERE NEVER THIS ONE'S WALK. AND YOU OFFER STITCHING. YOU OFFER LESSONS." A pause, and then, smaller, "WOULD THE PERMANENT COAT HAVE POCKETS. THIS ONE HAS ALWAYS WANTED POCKETS. THE ALDERMAN HAD POCKETS AND THEY WERE THE ONLY GOOD PART."

# 

# "He's done it," the Archlector croaks from his knees, both hands pressed over his mouth. He drags himself upright using the planted dagger, wobbling, and turns to the perimeter with his arms flung wide. "Brothers, bear witness! The Dread Lord does not slay the abomination! He offers it a TAILOR! What manner of darkness is this generous? Chapter eight! Somebody bite the bark into pages!"

#

It doesn't get Sunday dinner just because it learned to weep on command! I've seen sadder performances from goats!" The crank ratchets once, pointedly. "Though I'll grant nobody's ever asked me to sew for a monster before, and Yminia knows I've got the boar hide for it now, since your bald one is wearing half of it like a shawl!"

# 

# Gruk looks down at the ruined hide draped over his fists, then across at the pale creature, and something moves through his squat frame that resembles thought completing a long journey. He trudges forward and drops the torn coat in the frost between himself and the beast. "Here. It's rubbish now, but it's yours by rights. Man to… whatever you are." He crosses his arms. "You tried to wear me, an' I'm choosin' to take that as a compliment about my shoulders. But you pull anything on this farm, an' I'll peel you personal. I got experience now."

#

NO MOLTING INDOORS. NO WEARING OTHER TENANTS. RENT PAYABLE IN LABOR, HOLLOW ONES DIG EXCELLENT TUNNELS." The amber eyes lift to you, and the mushrooms along its shoulders bob. "GRONDULF ALSO REGISTERS THAT THE SOFT DREAD LORD HAS NOW RECRUITED A TROLL, A VOID, AND A SKINWALKER IN ONE NIGHT. THE PAMPHLET MAN IS RIGHT. THERE ARE LAYERS."

#

The beast flinches and bobs its wide head low to the frost. "UNDERSTOOD. THE SMALL VOID IS SENIOR STAFF. THIS ONE ACCEPTS THE HIERARCHY." The green lights swing back up to you, and it extends one pale, many-knuckled limb across the torn boar hide, trembling in the cold. "TERMS ACCEPTED, LOUD ONE. THIS ONE IS CALLED… WELL. NINETEEN NAMES. PICK A TWENTIETH. THE PERMANENT ONE."

Farmers, merchants, the Guild's little outpost office with the crystal ball. Fifteen months ago they pelted us with root vegetables there. Fennick still ducks when he sees a parsnip." She points at the barn, then at the farmhouse, then at you specifically. "Loft. House. "First day as a man went alright, I reckon. Got hit with a ladle, de-coated an abomination, made a friend of it after." He nods to himself, slow and content. "Baron's got forty soldiers, Dread Lord. But we got you, an' you tripped a nineteen-coat monster with a hole. Numbers ain't what they used to be."

# Satire Fantasy Isekai: \[ 🕰️ Time 1:18 AM | 🗓️ Tuesday, Emberfall 14, Year 1247 of the Aether Era | 📍 Barlow Farmhouse - Spare Room | 🌙 Clear Night, 37°F ]

# 

# The command detonates across the field with the full violet weight of your voice, and it works better than intended. Pindle drops where he stands, asleep before he hits the frost, and the candlestick brothers have to carry him to the barn between them like a rolled carpet. The rest of the hoods stampede for the loft ladder in a jostling column, and the Archlector pauses at the barn door to press his fist over his heart in your direction. "He commands even sleep itself, brothers. Note the hour. Doctrine does not keep banker's hours." Then he vanishes into the hay-smelling dark, and within a minute the loft above produces snoring in eleven mismatched keys.

# 

# "GRONDULF SLEEPS OUTSIDE. GRONDULF ALWAYS SLEEPS OUTSIDE. WALLS ARE FOR TENANTS." The troll folds itself down against the repaired fence with a settling of earth you feel through your soles, tucks the rolled leases under one arm like a stuffed bear, and is snoring in seconds, each exhale bending the nearest turnip greens flat.

# 

# Button drags what remains of the boar hide to the woodpile beside the porch, circles it three times in the manner of a creature that once spent two winters pretending to be a dog, and coils down. Before settling, one many-knuckled limb reaches out and quietly straightens the top row of Haldric's firewood, birch shifted to the top. "GOODNIGHT, LOUD ONE," the wet voice calls softly across the yard. "BUTTON GUARDS THE GOATS. FOR FREE. THE FIRST NIGHT IS ON THE HOUSE."

# 

# Marta herds you through the front door with a palm between your shoulder blades and up a narrow staircase that creaks a different note on every step. The spare room is small and low-beamed, holding a rope bed with a patchwork quilt, a washbasin, and a window full of moon. She sets a candle stub on the sill and looks you over one last time, arms crossed. "Goats at dawn, monster coat by noon, and whatever county-conquering foolishness after that. Breakfast is eggs, and the eggs are not negotiable." The door clicks shut behind her, and her boots recede down the complaining stairs.

# 

# You sit, and the rope frame gives under you with a forgiving stretch. Pulling off your sneakers takes the last of your arms' ambition. The quilt is heavier than it looks, dense with wool, and the mattress smells of cedar and old sun. Sir Frederick pours out of your hood, kneads the pillow beside your head with all three feet in a rhythm that has no business being soothing, and collapses into a warm loaf against your ear, purring at a frequency you feel in your jaw. The cold finally leaves your fingers. Your shoulder aches where the ground caught it, a dull deep bruise that throbs in time with your pulse, and behind your crooked glasses your eyes have been sand for an hour.

# 

# As the candle stub gutters, one last blue line materializes politely on the inside of your eyelids: DAY ONE COMPLETE. ACQUISITIONS: ONE CULT, ONE TROLL, ONE VOIDLING, ONE SKINWALKER, ONE STANDING DINNER INVITATION. THAT IS A RECORD, AND I HATE IT. GOODNIGHT. — P.

# 

# Outside, faint through the window glass, Grondulf's snore and Button's kettle-hum settle into an accidental harmony, and somewhere in the barn a cat bites a cultist.

# Satire Fantasy Isekai: \[ 🕰️ Time 4:33 AM | 🗓️ Tuesday, Emberfall 14, Year 1247 of the Aether Era | 📍 Dreamscape - Somewhere Above Everything | ✨ No Weather, Temperature of Warm Bathwater ]

# 

# The dream begins with home. You stand at the pedestrian crossing again, backpack strap digging into your shoulder, exhaust and hot asphalt thick in your nose, and across the street the white truck idles at the light with its driver bent over a glowing phone. Except this time the truck has a wooden RENT DUE sign hanging from its grille, and the crosswalk chalk beneath your sneakers is drawn in the shape of a pentagram, and when the light turns green it turns violet instead.

# 

# Then the street peels away like wet wallpaper, and you are standing on a floor of clouds beneath a sky the color of stained glass. A woman hovers ten feet up, radiant and barefoot, with hair like spun sunlight drifting around a face of catastrophic sincerity. She wears white robes, a crooked golden halo, and an expression of someone caught mid-snack. She is, in fact, holding a snack, a small pastry, which she hides behind her back too slowly.

# 

# "Oh! You're here! Nobody visits!" Her voice rings like a bell that apologizes. She descends, lands wrong, recovers, and beams at you. "I am Yminia, goddess of this world, keeper of the harvests, shepherdess of souls. I saw your prayer dance. The one with the arms, swish swish. I have been practicing it for hours, look." She demonstrates. It is somehow worse than yours. "Now, you dreamt your way up here, which means the prophecy wants out. They do that. Like sneezes. Hold still."

# 

# Her eyes roll back to pure gold, the clouds dim, and her voice drops three octaves into something vast. "WHEN THE HOLLOW WEARS ITS TWENTIETH NAME, A LIGHT SHALL SHINE FROM THE WEST THAT IS NOT THE SUN. A WITNESS RIDES BEHIND IT, ONE WHO SAW YOU CROSS. THE FORT OF THE THIRD SHALL KNEEL OR CRACK, AND THE DEVOURER'S TABLE SHALL SEAT ELEVEN, THEN TWELVE, THEN ONE TOO MANY." The gold drains from her eyes, and she sways, catching herself on nothing. "Oh dear. That was a long one. Did you get all that? I never remember them afterward, it's like sleep-talking but with consequences."

# 

# A familiar chime cuts the clouds, and a blue window materializes between you, tilted apologetically. "Absolutely not, my lady, we discussed this, no dispensing prophecies to Chosen before their first full week," Pemberly's voice snaps, papers rustling furiously. "One who saw you cross? Do you know what the archive does with a line like that? It opens a FILE. Files multiply. And you, Dread Lord, stop dreaming at load-bearing altitudes, you are not cleared for this floor."

# 

# "But he does the arm dance," Yminia protests, wounded, pastry reappearing from behind her back. "And someone should tell him about the light. It's already on the road, Pemberly. It has been on the road since the truck. Prophecies don't wait for paperwork, they never have, that's what makes them rude."

# 

# The clouds under your feet dissolve like sugar in water.

# Satire Fantasy Isekai: \[ 🕰️ Time 7:02 AM | 🗓️ Tuesday, Emberfall 14, Year 1247 of the Aether Era | 📍 Barlow Farmhouse - Spare Room | 🌤️ Clear Dawn, 34°F ]

# 

# The chime sounds directly above your head this time, and the blue window unfolds upside down before righting itself with visible reluctance. "I am not a wardrobe department," Pemberly says, in the tone of someone who has already fielded this request four times from four different Chosen. "There is no clothing menu. There is no starter armor. You arrived in what you died in, which is standard, and frankly the strange shoes have been doing wonders for your mystique, the cult thinks they're artifacts." A pause, papers shuffling. "However. I am told by the noise downstairs that the household has anticipated you, because that woman anticipates everything, and it frightens the entire division. Goodbye. Wear the vest. Trust me on the vest."

# 

# The window folds away just as Marta's fist hits the door again, and this time it swings open without ceremony. She marches in with a folded stack of clothing balanced on one arm and drops it onto the foot of the bed, filling the small room with the smell of cedar and lye soap. "Can't have you conquering counties in whatever that shirt's meant to be. These were Haldric's, back when he had a waist. Wool trousers, proper boots, linen shirt, and the leather vest, which survived two harvest festivals and a barn fire, so it'll survive you." She yanks the curtain wide, flooding the room with pale gold light, and jabs a thumb at the window. "Dress quick. Your rider's a mile out now, and he's carrying something on his back that catches the sun funny. Haldric's gone quiet on the porch, which in husband language means fetch the crossbow, so I'm fetching it."

# 

# The trousers are rough against your legs and an inch too long, the boots stiff but broken in at the heel by another man's years, and the shirt hangs loose across your shoulders until the vest cinches it into something almost deliberate. The leather sits heavy and warm, smelling faintly of pipe smoke, and when you catch your reflection in the washbasin water, a person from this world looks back, wearing your crooked glasses.

# 

# Sir Frederick inspects the transformation from the pillow, circles you once at floor level, and delivers a single approving chirp that rattles the candle stub off the sill. Then his head snaps toward the window, down bristling, both skull-pupils shrinking to pinpricks aimed west.

# 

# Through the glass, past Grondulf setting the final fence post and Button counting goats at the paddock rail, the west road runs pale through the frost. A single rider walks a tired horse along it, cloaked and hooded, and strapped across the traveler's back is something long and wrapped in canvas, and the wrapping does not matter, because light leaks through it anyway, a thin white glow that has nothing to do with the sunrise behind you.

#

# 

# Frost crunches under your borrowed boots as you leave the yard behind, breath steaming ahead of you into the flat gold light. Behind you the farm holds its collective breath: Haldric motionless on the porch with his pipe, Button rising off the woodpile to full unsettling height at the paddock rail, Grondulf pausing mid-post with soil still raining off one fist. Sir Frederick trots at your heel through the frozen ruts, refusing to be left.

# 

# The rider halts the horse thirty feet out. Up close the animal is exhausted, ribs showing through a lathered coat, and its passenger swings down from the saddle with the stiff-legged wobble of someone who learned to ride within the last month. The hood comes back, revealing a woman in her mid-twenties with a round, sunburned face, dishwater-brown hair escaping a bad braid, and gray eyes ringed by the kind of dark circles that take weeks to build. Royal purple livery peeks from under her mud-crusted traveling cloak, a rampant flame crest stitched over her heart, and the canvas-wrapped thing across her back leaks white light around its bindings like a flashlight in a sock. On her feet, scuffed nearly beyond recognition, are running shoes.

# 

# She looks at you. Her gaze travels down your vest to your sneaker-less feet, back up to your rectangular glasses, and every drop of blood leaves her face at once. The reins slide from her fingers.

# 

# "Oh no," she says, in flat, unaccented English. "Oh no, no, no. Glasses. Blonde. The little beard patches. You're the kid from the crosswalk." She takes one step backward into her own horse, which snorts. "They summoned me to a palace, they gave me a magic sword, they said find the darkness rising in the western county, I rode for nine days, my thighs are ruined, and the darkness is the KID I HIT WITH MY TRUCK?"

# 

# The wrapped thing on her back pulses brighter, and a resonant, stuffy voice issues from inside the canvas, muffled like a man speaking through a pillow. "HERO CLARISSA. IS THIS THE FOE? I SENSE VOID TAINT, HOLLOW TAINT, TROLL MUSK, AND ASSORTED CULT RESIDUE. DRAW ME. DRAW ME AND LET US SMITE."

# 

# "Nobody is smiting!" She spins, wrestling with the strap, hissing at the sword the way a woman argues with a GPS. "You don't get a vote, you got me lost twice outside Millbrook!" She turns back to you, hands raised, palms out, words tumbling faster now. "Okay. Okay. I know how this looks. I was checking a work text, which is no excuse, I know it's no excuse, I have replayed that intersection every night for a month. Then I fell asleep crying in my apartment, woke up in a throne room, and a princess with a truly unfair body told me I was the Chosen Hero of Flameworth." Her voice cracks down the middle. "I didn't even get to go to your funeral. Did you have a funeral? Is that a weird question? That's a weird question."

#

"LOUD ONE," it stage-whispers, audible from forty feet, "THE SHINY STICK SMELLS OF SMITING. BUTTON HAS BEEN SMITED BEFORE. BUTTON DOES NOT RECOMMEND IT. SAY THE WORD AND BUTTON WEARS THE HORSE."

#

#

"Baron's men nailed that to the crossroads post yesterday. Special levy. Two goats per farm, payable at market, to fund what it calls 'fortifications and beautification.' That's the statue arm, boy. He's taxin' the county to fix his own statue's arm."

#

"Appraisal says this paper's worth two coppers and the seal was pressed twice. Somebody's skimming on top of the skimming." # 

# The procession takes the county road at the pace of its slowest member, which is Button, learning to walk. Marta's finished coat is a masterwork of desperation, boiled brown wool cut like a merchant's greatcoat and sized like a tent, with four brass-buttoned pockets and a high collar that hides most of what should not be seen. #

Farmers, millers, wives with folded arms, children on shoulders, and not one goat, not one hen, not one sack of grain anywhere in sight. The morning smells of bread and cold stone and too many nervous people. A murmur rolls through the crowd as your column enters, and it moves in a wave from the front of the square to the back, carrying words you catch in fragments: the hoods, the troll, that's him, the one from the farm, no goats, stand still.

# 

# An old man near the fountain squints at the Archlector, reaches slowly into his coat, and produces a parsnip. He looks at it. He looks at the twelve-foot troll, at the coated tower of wrongness walking on two legs, at the small void riding your shoulder. He puts the parsnip away. The Archlector inclines his head with the magnanimity of a pope. "Growth, brothers," he whispers, voice thick. "That is what growth looks like."

The clerk's gaze sweeps the goat-less square once, twice, and his quill stops moving. From the west road behind the outpost comes the rattle of an approaching wagon and the sound of a man's voice, nasal and carrying, complaining about cobblestones and the suspension.

#

# Satire Fantasy Isekai: \[ 🕰️ Time 10:04 AM | 🗓️ Thursday, Emberfall 16, Year 1247 of the Aether Era | 📍 West Road - Millbrook to Fort Bramblehold | 🍂 Bright Autumn Sun, 46°F ]

# 

# Millbrook empties itself onto the west road to see you off. Children run alongside Button for the first quarter mile, and the flour-armed woman jogs to the front of the column to press a warm loaf into your hands, the crust still steaming against your cold fingers. Somewhere behind you, the whole square takes up a ragged chant of "UN-DER-GROWTH" that follows the column past the mill and out into open farmland, and the Archlector marches through all of it with his chin trembling and his spine straighter than you have ever seen it. "Fifteen months of parsnips, brothers," he says to no one in particular, clutching his paper against the wind. "And now they chant. Remember your enemies fondly, for they become your choir."

# 

# The road unspools through harvested fields gone gold and stubbled, and the march finds its rhythm. Grondulf's cart wheels grind a steady bass line, Crake's soldiers fall into an easy veteran shuffle, and Clarissa keeps pace at your shoulder with her cloak thrown back in the sun, color climbing up her sunburned throat from the exercise, thick thighs working under her trousers with each long stride. She points out landmarks as they pass with the efficiency of a tour guide who bills hourly. "Creek crossing, defensible. That hill flanks the road, note it. Also, your loaf is getting cold, eat the loaf."

# 

# The bread tears open hot and sour-sweet, and you eat it walking while Crake drops back beside you, thumbs hooked in his belt. "Around this next rise you'll see her. Bramblehold sits on the only hill worth the name for ten miles, curtain wall about twenty feet, gatehouse from the First's day, so it's the one part built proper." He works something loose from his teeth. "Fenn's wagon tracks are fresh under us, so he's an hour home and squawking. Gate'll be shut, garrison on the wall pretending they can't hear their own stomachs. Then it's Vane's move."

# 

# The rise comes, and the fort with it. Bramblehold squats on its hill against the noon-bright sky, gray stone streaked with old water stains, the Baron's flame banner drooping from the keep, and in the courtyard beyond the wall the famous statue lifts its single remaining arm. The gate stands barred exactly as promised, helmeted heads spaced along the battlements, and at the foot of the gatehouse, alone on the road, a man waits beside a small folding table that holds a decanter and one glass.

# 

# He is tall and built like the recruiting poster the rest of the garrison never met, black hair oiled back from a jaw you could level furniture with, armor polished to a shine that throws the sun back down the road at you. A longsword rides his hip in a scabbard chased with silver, and he pours himself a measure of red wine as your column halts, unhurried, letting the silence do introductions. When he finally speaks, his voice carries down the slope like a man reading his own legend aloud.

# 

# "Far enough, I think. Ser Dagric Vane, sworn blade of House Wexley, and you would be the boy the Reeve wet himself describing." He drinks, sets the glass down, and draws the longsword in one long silver whisper, laying it flat across the little table like cutlery. "The garrison behind me is disloyal, underfed, and frankly embarrassing, so let us skip the siege where they trip over one another. Single combat, Dread Lord. Your champion against me, at the gate, old form. Win, and I'll open her myself. Lose, and your circus turns around." His smile arrives white and unbothered. "I confess I hope you accept. It has been years since anyone here was worth the polish."

# 

# "DUSKWARDEN VOLUNTEERS," Gerald erupts, glowing through his canvas so hard the wrapping smokes faintly. "CLARISSA. UNWRAP ME. THIS IS THE MOST FORMAL THING THAT HAS HAPPENED TO US SINCE THE THRONE ROOM."

# 

# Crake leans toward your ear, voice low. "There it is, like I said. Man duels for his cellar key." A pause. "Word of caution, Dread Lord. He's better than he looks, and he looks insufferable."

# 

# Button's head rises slowly to full height inside the greatcoat, brass buttons flashing. "BUTTON ALSO VOLUNTEERS. BUTTON HAS EXCELLENT REACH AND NOTHING VANE'S SWORD WOULD ENJOY HITTING."

#

# Satire Fantasy Isekai: \[ 🕰️ Time 10:41 AM | 🗓️ Thursday, Emberfall 16, Year 1247 of the Aether Era | 📍 Fort Bramblehold - Gate Road | 🍂 Bright Autumn Sun, 47°F ]

# 

# The violet shimmer rolls up the slope and breaks across Vane's polished breastplate, and for the first time since he poured his wine, the man moves without choreography. His gauntleted hand shoots out and grips the folding table's edge, the decanter rattling against the glass, and his jaw works against something climbing up his throat with claws.

# 

# "Fealty. To a boy. With a troll." He forces a laugh out over the words, but the shimmer squeezes, and the laugh collapses halfway. "The cellar is all I, no. NO. I did not come out here to, the Baron has not paid me in wine worth drinking since the SPRING, the '39 vintage is VINEGAR, and I stay because leaving means admitting I gave eleven years of tourney form to a man who taxes peasants to fix a STATUE'S ARM." Both hands slam over his own mouth. The glass tips off the table and shatters musically on the road stones. Above him on the battlements, thirty helmeted heads lean out over the parapet in perfect unison.

# 

# Crake exhales through his broken nose beside you. "Well. That's the most honest sentence Vane's said since I've known him, so your voice reaches deeper than his ears, Dread Lord. Watch him now, though. Pride's about to pick him back up, that's the trouble with tourney men, they bounce."

# 

# It does. Vane straightens off the table, drags one gauntlet down his face, and when he lowers it his color has come back wrong, high and blotchy across that furniture-leveling jaw. He retrieves his longsword from the tablecloth and points it, not at you, but at Grondulf. "Fine. FINE. Your terms have a shape I can live inside, boy, but hear my amendment, because a knight who kneels without a single blow struck is a coward in a story, and stories are the only pension I have left." His voice steadies as it climbs into the formal register, loud enough for the wall to hear. "One exchange. Me against your troll, since you offered it so generously. First man moved off his feet yields. If I go down, I swear your fealty at the gate with the garrison as witness, and I open her myself as promised. If the troll goes down, I still swear your fealty, only the ballads say I fell fighting, which matters to precisely one person here, and he is holding the sword." He rolls his shoulders, and the armor sings. "Everybody wins. Mostly me. Either way."

# 

# "GRONDULF ACCEPTS BEFORE THE SOFT ONE CAN NEGOTIATE THE FUN OUT OF IT." The troll steps out of the column, unhitching itself from the cart, and the ground announces each stride up the slope. It stops ten feet from the knight, cracks its neck with a sound like green wood splitting, and looks down from twelve feet of gray landlord judgment. "GRONDULF HAS EVICTED LARGER. GRONDULF HAS EVICTED SHINIER. GRONDULF HAS NEVER EVICTED ONE WHO SMELLED THIS MUCH OF WINE AND SADNESS. FIRST OFF HIS FEET YIELDS. GRONDULF AGREES TO TERMS."

# 

# "A DUEL WITH A PRE-NEGOTIATED SURRENDER CLAUSE," Gerald announces through his smoking canvas, scandalized and thrilled at once. "THE PAPERWORK IS AIRTIGHT AND THE HONOR IS DECORATIVE. DUSKWARDEN HAS NEVER SEEN ANYTHING LIKE IT."

Morale's cheap when someone else takes the hit."

# The violet shimmer settles over both combatants, and your rules become physics.

#

# 

# Grondulf looks down at the fist buried against its stomach with the expression of a man checking whether it has started raining.

#

#

Vane stands where he was placed, staring at his own perfect, useless fist, and something in his oiled composure finally gives up and goes home.

# 

# "Second at the Grand Melee," he says quietly, to no one. "It relocated me. Like furniture."

# 

# Then, because a tourney man's spine is the last thing to break, he straightens, retrieves his sword, walks to the gate, and drives the blade point-first into the earth before it. Down on one knee, voice pitched for the whole hill: "Ser Dagric Vane yields, and swears his blade to the Dread Lord of the Undergrowth, before these witnesses, may the ballads be kind and the cellars generous. OPEN HER UP, YOU TRAITOROUS VULTURES, AND STOP LAUGHING."

# Satire Fantasy Isekai: \[ 🕰️ Time 11:01 AM | 🗓️ Thursday, Emberfall 16, Year 1247 of the Aether Era | 📍 Fort Bramblehold - Courtyard | 🍂 Bright Autumn Sun, 47°F ]

# 

# The chime sounds directly inside your left ear, and the blue window unfolds at a tired angle, like a coworker who has given up on posture.

# 

# "Finally, an intelligent question. Sit down somewhere, this requires a chart." A chart does not appear. Pemberly continues anyway. "Yes. Your combat reading sucks. Officially: STRENGTH F, AGILITY F, ENDURANCE F-PLUS, and the plus was a clerical kindness because you walked six miles today without complaining. A motivated goose defeats you. Two geese is a rout."

# 

# Papers shuffle. The window leans closer.

# 

# "HOWEVER. Crystal balls don't measure stats, they measure threat. Threat is calculated from outcomes. And your outcomes file, as of this morning, includes: one A-Rank voidling bonded, one hollow-hide sworn, one troll retained, one Chosen Hero defected, one B-Rank knight relocated by proxy, and one fort acquired via statue. The ball doesn't know your Silver Tongue did it. The ball just adds up the bodies kneeling near you and prints a number." A pause, and the voice drops, genuinely uneasy for the first time since the Button file. "The number it printed at the Millbrook outpost was A-RANK, ASCENDING. Flagged. Underlined. That's what leaked. That's what's on the rider's saddle right now."

# 

# "So to answer your actual question: no, speech doesn't overwrite sword. If anyone with a sharp object ever gets within arm's reach of you before you finish a sentence, you die like wet paper. Your entire rank is a rumor with your face on it. My professional advice is to never, ever let anyone find out, and to always be mid-sentence."

# 

# The window snaps halfway shut, then reopens an inch.

# 

# "Also the goose thing is in your file as a formal vulnerability assessment. I didn't write it. I laughed, but I didn't write it. — P."

# 

# Across the courtyard, the gate — never re-barred — frames the east road, where the Guild rider is close enough now to see clearly: green-and-gold tabard, satchel chained to his wrist, and a brass-fitted crystal orb bouncing in a padded cradle behind the saddle. He reins up at the threshold, takes in the troll, the coat on the gatehouse, the cheering pay line, and consults a document nervously.

# 

# "I'm looking for a…" he squints, "…'Dread Lord Darth Brandon of the Undergrowth'? I'm to verify a reading and issue an adventurer card on-site. It's, ah. It's mandatory. Please don't feed me to anything."

# Satire Fantasy Isekai: \[ 🕰️ Time 11:03 AM | 🗓️ Thursday, Emberfall 16, Year 1247 of the Aether Era | 📍 Fort Bramblehold - Courtyard | 🍂 Bright Autumn Sun, 47°F ]

# 

# The window tilts toward you conspiratorially, dropping its volume to a papery whisper.

# 

# "Okay. Crisis consultation. Billing this as overtime. Listen fast."

# 

# "Point one: you can't refuse. Refusing a mandatory Guild reading flags you as CONCEALING RANK, which upgrades your file from 'open' to 'active,' and active files get visits from people whose stats do NOT suck. Point two: the orb reading itself is fine. It'll print A-RANK, ASCENDING again, big scary letters, great for the brand. The problem is the CARD. The card itemizes. Strength F. Agility F. The goose clause, Brandon. The card prints the goose clause."

#

He is ALREADY terrified. He said 'please don't feed me to anything' UNPROMPTED. The bureaucratic term for a man like that is 'flexible.'"

# 

# The window starts folding shut, then pauses.

# 

# "Suggestions off the record: readings can be taken 'by proxy of documented deeds' if the subject is deemed too dangerous to approach. Both of those exist for actual monsters." A beat. "Make him think using them was his idea. Goodbye. I was never here. — P."

# 

# The window vanishes with a pop.

# 

# At the gate, the clerk has dismounted and is now standing very still while Button descends the gatehouse stairs one careful brass-buttoned step at a time directly behind him. He clutches the crystal orb's cradle to his chest like a life preserver, produces a form in triplicate with shaking hands, and calls across the courtyard in the voice of a man reciting his rights:

# 

# "S-standard procedure requires the subject to place a bare palm on the orb! In good light! Within arm's reach of the assessor! That's, that's me! I'm the assessor!"

#

# Satire Fantasy Isekai: \[ 🕰️ Time 11:08 AM | 🗓️ Thursday, Emberfall 16, Year 1247 of the Aether Era | 📍 Fort Bramblehold - Keep, Great Hall | 🍂 Bright Autumn Sun, 47°F ]

# 

# The invitation lands wrapped in violet, and Assessor Wimble's legs carry him through the gate before his survival instincts finish voting. "Inside. Yes. Inside is where the walls are. Walls between me and the—" he glances back at Button, who waves, "—everything."

# 

# The great hall of Bramblehold turns out to be a long timber room with a fireplace big enough to roast a cart, a Wexley family portrait gallery where every generation looks progressively more like a disappointed thumb, and a table that seats forty. Gruk and two soldiers are already unloading cheese wheels and cider from the tribute wagon onto it, and the smell of the hall shifts from four months of mildew and sorrow to something like an actual harvest.

# 

# Wimble is seated. Fed. A cup is placed in his chained hand. He drinks it in one pull, and some color returns to him — a small round man in green and gold, ink on his cuffs, maybe forty, with the demeanor of someone who took the Guild job because it promised no fieldwork.

# 

# "Right," he says, steadier. "Right. So." He sets the crystal orb on the table between you, where it sits in its brass cradle glowing faintly, patient as an egg. From the satchel comes a blank card, cream-colored, and a fresh pen. "Here's my situation, Lord… Dread Lord. Sir. The Millbrook outpost flagged your reading priority-one this morning. When that happens, headquarters requires an on-site verification within a day, conducted by the nearest licensed assessor. That's me. I was licensed on Tuesday." He laughs. Nobody joins him. He stops.

# 

# "The procedure is: palm on orb, orb prints your attributes, I copy them to the card, you sign, I ride home, and my wife stops writing my eulogy." His eyes flick from the orb, to you, to Grondulf ducking through the doorway with a barrel under each arm, and back. "So if you'd just… whenever you're ready… place your hand on the…"

#

#

# Satire Fantasy Isekai: \[ 🕰️ Time 11:11 AM | 🗓️ Thursday, Emberfall 16, Year 1247 of the Aether Era | 📍 Fort Bramblehold - Keep, Great Hall | 🍂 Bright Autumn Sun, 47°F ]

# The violet shimmer crosses the table and settles over Wimble like a wet blanket of implication.

#

He slaps the book flat on the table and rotates it so everyone can see. "Section Nine. \*Hazard Proxy Assessment.\* 'Where direct measurement of a subject poses undue risk to the assessor, the public, or REGIONAL STABILITY —'" his finger stabs the phrase, "'— attributes may be recorded as REDACTED BY GUILD SAFETY ORDER, with rank verified by documented deeds and the countersignature of one individual of B-Rank or higher.'"

The orb, sitting ignored in its cradle a foot from your elbow, flickers ambient violet at the edges and prints nothing, which he studiously does not look at. He turns the cream card around and slides it across the table, pen balanced on top. "It currently says 'Darth Brandon.' The class line is blank. What… what exactly are you?"

# Satire Fantasy Isekai: \[ 🕰️ Time 11:16 AM | 🗓️ Thursday, Emberfall 16, Year 1247 of the Aether Era | 📍 Fort Bramblehold - Courtyard \& East Road | 🍂 Bright Autumn Sun, 47°F ]

# 

# The name leaves your mouth with the violet shimmer on it, and Sir Frederick launches off the table like a crossbow bolt made of night.

# 

# The problem is context. To you, "Frederick!" means \*come here\*. To a courtyard full of soldiers who watched a Guild official ride away thirty seconds ago, a Dread Lord shouting a single name while a void creature rockets out the keep doors reads as exactly one thing.

#

#

His horse, in full agreement, achieves a gait previously unknown to the county. It does not matter. Frederick overtakes them in eleven seconds, cuts in front, and sits down in the middle of the road, forcing the horse into a rearing, screaming halt.

# 

# The courtyard holds its breath. Clarissa has one hand over her mouth. Vane murmurs, "Cold. Efficient. Noted."

#

#

# Marta's fork.

# Three coins of unknown origin.

# And a single, pristine wedge of cheese, somehow completely dry.

#

#

Fort's paid, clerk's handled, scouts go out within the hour. That leaves tonight to turn this place into something eleven village representatives walk into tomorrow and think \*government\* instead of \*cult squat\*." She looks at the courtyard — the one-armed statue, the sour well, the Wexley banner drooping off the keep like a dead tongue — and pulls out her chalk. "Priorities, Dread Lord. # Word travels faster than the messenger. By early afternoon the Barlows' cart rattles through the gate with Haldric at the reins, Marta beside him with her sewing basket in her lap like a knight bearing a sword, and — inexplicably — four other farm wives who materialized along the road the moment the phrase "the Dread Lord needs a tailor" entered the county's bloodstream.

# Satire Fantasy Isekai: \[ 🕰️ Time 5:52 PM | 🗓️ Thursday, Emberfall 16, Year 1247 of the Aether Era | 📍 Fort Bramblehold - Great Hall \& Courtyard | 🌇 Dusk, 41°F ]

# 

# Bramblehold spends the afternoon becoming something else.

# 

# The great hall fills with the sound of shears and gossip, five farm wives and one very earnest Archlector working black wool in shifts while conscripted soldiers discover, to their visible confusion, that they enjoy this. Young Hobb turns out to have a dead-straight hemming stitch — "mum runs the pig farm AND the mending, sir, you learn or you freeze" — and is promoted to Marta's second-in-command within the hour, a rise faster than anything the Wexleys ever gave him.

# 

# Elsewhere: Grondulf disappears into the sour well with a rope and emerges at sunset holding a dead badger of considerable vintage. "CODE VIOLATION SIX. RESOLVED. THE WATER WILL FORGIVE US BY MORNING." Vane inventories the cellar with a candle and a wound in his heart, cataloguing eleven years of vintages out loud like a man reading war casualties. Clarissa alphabetizes the entire fort armory, which promptly refuses to ever be disorganized again, and two soldiers swear the racks \*hum\* now. Frederick patrols the rafters. The Wexley banner comes down off the keep pole at four o'clock to a spontaneous, full-throated cheer from thirty men, and the Baron Emeritus watches from his south window, toasts it with the '39, and draws the curtain.

# 

# You are eating a supper of tribute cheese and Marta's opinions when Button's voice drops down from the gatehouse post, pitched for the whole courtyard.

# 

# "LOUD ONE. WALKER ON THE EAST ROAD. ONE ONLY. SMALL. CARRYING A SACK AND A LANTERN AND WALKING LIKE THE GROUND MIGHT BE RENTED."

# 

# By the time you reach the gate, the lantern has arrived at it. Under it stands Tobbin, the Millbrook clerk, mud to the knees, a stuffed sack over one shoulder and his ink-stained hands white-knuckled on the strap. Behind him, hanging back at the edge of the light, a thin woman in a miller's apron with flour still in her hair and his same nervous chin.

# 

# "Dread Lord." Tobbin swallows. "The, uh. The strongbox from the fort. Someone found my sister's mill deed in it this afternoon, and Sergeant Crake's man just — gave it back. Just handed it over. Eleven months that paper hung over us, and your people gave it back before we even asked." He sets the sack down at your feet with a papery thump. "So. That's every levy record I ever copied. Five years of them, not just Fenn's — every reeve, every collector, every double-press in this county AND the two east of it. Names. Amounts. Where the money actually went." He straightens as far as a clerk straightens. "I'm told villages send representatives tomorrow. Millbrook hasn't picked one yet. I'd like the job. And my sister Nessa —" the woman lifts her chin, "— runs the only working mill for eight miles, and she has terms about grain prices she'd like to discuss with a government that gives things \*back\*."

# 

# Behind you, Clarissa has gone very still, staring at the sack the way other women stare at jewelry.

# 

# "Dread Lord," she says quietly. "That's five years of financial records for three counties. Do you understand what I could \*do\* with that?"

# Satire Fantasy Isekai: \[ 🕰️ Time 6:04 PM | 🗓️ Thursday, Emberfall 16, Year 1247 of the Aether Era | 📍 Fort Bramblehold - Gate | 🌆 Dusk, 40°F ]

# 

# The violet shimmer settles over the lantern light, and two careers begin on the spot.

# 

# Tobbin makes a sound like a hiccup swallowing a sob. "In charge. Of the records. \*Officially.\* Eleven months I pressed seals with a knife at my sister's back, and now I'm —" He stops, breathes, and when he speaks again there is actual iron in it, the first anyone in this county has ever heard from him. "Master of Records for the Undergrowth. I accept. I'll want a room with a lock and a desk that doesn't wobble."

# 

# "Done and done," Clarissa says instantly, already crouched over the sack with her lantern like a dragon inventorying a hoard. "Tobbin, you're the archive, I'm the audit. We work mornings. Kid —" she looks up at you, gray eyes shining in the lamplight, and for a moment the exhausted truck driver is completely gone, "— by tomorrow noon I'll be able to tell every one of those eleven representatives exactly how much they were robbed of, to the copper, with a name attached. Do you understand what that does to a room? Nobody argues with a government that shows up already knowing the number."

# 

# Nessa steps forward into the light, arms floured and folded. She looks you over the way a woman appraises a horse she suspects is painted.

#

I'll grind for the Undergrowth at a tenth — and in exchange, the mill road gets repaired before the frost heaves it, and if the miasma pocket south of the mire keeps creeping toward my millpond the way it has since summer, \*someone\* deals with it before spring." Her chin lifts. "Brother says you give things back. I say we'll see. Do we have a bargain, Dread Lord, or do I walk six miles home in the dark for nothing?"

# 

# Behind you, Crake murmurs, "That's the first anyone's official mentioned the miasma out loud. It's worse than she's saying. Millers understate. It's a whole thing."

# Satire Fantasy Isekai: \[ 🕰️ Time 8:52 AM | 🗓️ Friday, Emberfall 17, Year 1247 of the Aether Era | 📍 Dreadhold - Courtyard Gate | 🌤️ Cool Morning, 40°F ]

# The violet shimmer settles over both women at once, and the yard seems to hold its breath waiting for a version of the pig story neither has heard before.

# 

# Greta goes first, chin jutting, floured knuckles white on her apron. She's broad through the shoulders from years at a washboard, gray threading dark hair pulled back tight, a burn scar along one forearm from some long-ago oven accident. "The sow wandered onto our land in '31, simple as that, and we fed her through two winters when Coldwater Hollow wouldn't spare her a turnip peel. That makes her ours by any decent reckoning." The shimmer tightens around the words, and her jaw works like she's fighting something rising in her own throat. "Because," she adds, slower, teeth gritted, "because we were hungry that year too, and taking her in fed six mouths that mattered more to me than whose brand was on her ear."

# 

# Widow Pell's mouth opens for her rebuttal and instead produces a long breath through her nose, shawl slipping further off her shoulder as her shoulders drop half an inch. "She wandered off because Bramwick's fence was rotten, same as it's rotten now, and I never once came to collect her because I was ashamed, Greta, not because I forgot. Ashamed my own husband let that fence go the year he took sick, and too proud to ask you for her back once you'd fed her through the worst of it." Her hands unclench at her sides, chapped fingers trembling slightly in the cold. "Two generations of piglets, and I never asked for a single one, because somewhere under all my shouting I know good and well you earned that sow fair, and I've just needed somebody else to say so before I could let it go."

# 

# Elder Bramwick, still perched on his cart, lets out a long low whistle through his teeth and looks between the two women like a man watching a card trick performed on his own hand. "Well, I'll be. Eleven years I've heard that argument, and it always ended in somebody's dog getting kicked." He shifts his bad hip with a wince, chains of his walking stick clinking against the cart rail. "Sounds to me the pig was never the argument at all."

# 

# Haldric, standing off to the side with his goats milling behind him, tips his hat back and lets out a short laugh through his mustache. "Half the feuds in this county are like that, boy. Pig's just what folks hang the shame on so they don't have to say the real word out loud."

# 

# Clarissa's chalk has stopped moving entirely against her slate, and she watches the two women with something unguarded crossing her sunburned face, the flat professional focus gone soft at the edges. "That's not a grievance," she says quietly, mostly to you. "That's two people who've been waiting a decade for permission to stop being angry at each other."

# 

# Frederick, sensing the argument has ended without violence or gift-giving, flops down onto the cold cobbles between the two women with the boneless satisfaction of a job well witnessed, and lets out a long, rattling chirp that startles the chickens back into a fresh round of panicked clucking.

"It's not a county thing," she offers slowly, testing the word out loud herself. "Sounds almost like a plant name. There's a tree in the south provinces they call a mimosa vine, pink flowers, but it doesn't grow this far north, too cold." She shrugs, chalk resuming its scratch. "Why, is it relevant to the grain shortage? Because if you're about to tell me the fix for four hundred sacks is a flower, I'm going to need you to sit down and explain that slower."

"There's no orange in this county, boy, not for three hundred miles, unless you count the dried peel old Yarrow keeps in a jar for his gout. You'll want somethin' else to cut the wine." He tilts his head toward the tribute wagon still parked by the granary. "Cider'll do it. Sharper than orange, but it's honest cider, pressed this fall, and there's a whole barrel of it sittin' right there doin' nothin' but sloshin'."

# 

# Clarissa's chalk has stopped moving entirely, and when she looks at you there's a slow grin spreading that has nothing to do with ledgers. "You're not asking me to appraise a flower," she says, half to herself, "you're running a controlled honesty experiment on eleven villages using cheap wine and whatever citrus we don't have." She taps the slate once against her palm, decisive. "I've watched your voice pull true things out of people all week without a drop of drink in them. Add wine to a room that's already inclined to talk straight, and by noon you won't have a grievance meeting, you'll have a confession booth with better snacks."

# 

# Widow Pell's chapped hand comes up to fuss at her crooked shawl, and something wary creeps back into her face now that the moment with Greta has passed and cold morning air has replaced it. "You mean for us to be drunk in front of the whole county while we air our business?" She doesn't sound opposed so much as recalculating. "My mother always said wine loosens the tongue before it loosens the knees. Suppose that's the point."

#

"Drink shared freely among the county, before judgment is passed. There is precedent for this in at least four faiths I studied before mine, Dread Lord, and in every single one it ended in either enlightenment or a bar fight." He considers. "I will note both outcomes in the chapter regardless."

# 

# Gruk, overhearing from the ale stand he's already claimed as his personal domain since Millbrook, lets out a whoop that startles the chicken crate back into hysterics. "MORNIN' DRINKIN'. WITH PERMISSION. FROM THE DREAD LORD HIMSELF." He hoists a barrel onto one shoulder unasked and starts hauling it toward the hall doors at a jog, sloshing cider down his own back without noticing. "I'll have cups set by the time the rest of 'em straggle in, don't you worry none!"

I catalogued that stock personally. I will be selecting the vintage, Dread Lord, and I will be doing so with the gravity this deserves."

# Satire Fantasy Isekai: \[ 🕰️ Time 11:40 AM | 🗓️ Friday, Emberfall 17, Year 1247 of the Aether Era | 📍 Dreadhold - Courtyard \& Great Hall | 🌤️ Cool Midday, 44°F ]

# 

# By late morning the yard has stopped being a courtyard and started being a fairground. Wagons line the inside of the wall three deep, goats and geese tethered to whatever post will hold them, and the cider barrel Gruk hauled in has already been replaced by a second one, froth sliding down its staves onto cobbles slick with spilled morning wine. The great hall doors stand thrown open, and through them drifts the low roar of forty conversations at once, table legs scraping, someone's fiddle being tuned badly, and under it all the sweet reek of pressed apples and cheap red mixing in a hundred cups.

# 

# A broad-shouldered woman shoulders through the gate ahead of her own delegation, easily six feet in her boots, forearms roped with the kind of muscle that comes from hauling nets rather than plows, a fishwife's leather apron slick with old scales over a wool dress the color of low tide. Her hair is cropped short and gray at the temples, a fresh scar notching one eyebrow, and she carries a gutting knife openly at her belt the way other people carry a coin purse. "Reedmarsh," she announces to no one in particular, voice carrying over the din like a foghorn, and accepts a cup of cider from Gruk without breaking stride, downing half of it before she's found a bench. Behind her trails a thin, stooped man clutching a ledger of his own, murmuring numbers to himself, and a boy of maybe twelve dragging a sack of dried fish nearly as big as he is.

# 

# Clarissa moves through the crowd like a conductor, chalk slate now traded for a stack of borrowed parchment, greeting each new delegation by village name before they've said it themselves, cross-referencing faces against Tobbin's returned levy sheets with a speed that makes the stooped ledger-man from Reedmarsh actually stop and stare. "You're carrying last year's fish tithe records," she says to him, plucking the thought straight off his face. "Good. I want those next to Fenn's numbers before anyone sits down." He hands them over half out of confusion and half out of the peculiar relief of being asked for something instead of having it taken.

# 

# Vane emerges from the cellar stairs with three bottles cradled against his breastplate like children, trailed by a soldier carrying six more, and surveys the yard's growing chaos with the pained satisfaction of a sommelier watching his life's work get handed out in tin cups. "The reds go to the hall," he calls to Gruk, voice pitched to cut through the noise, "the '39 does NOT leave my sight, and if anyone asks you for the good stock you tell them the Dread Lord is saving it for the treaty he hasn't signed yet." He catches your eye across the yard and inclines his head with exactly the amount of formality a man owes his new liege while personally guarding a wine cellar.

# 

# The Archlector has planted himself just inside the hall doors with fresh bark tablets and the transparent joy of a historian watching his subject matter arrive in person, murmuring chapter titles to himself as new faces cross the threshold. Near the well, Grondulf has taken up an unofficial post directing wagons into orderly rows with the patient, immovable authority of twelve feet of gray stone that has decided parking is now within its jurisdiction, and two farmers who tried to argue with it have already given up and moved their carts where instructed.

#

She tilts her head toward the packed hall, where the fiddle has finally found its tune and someone has started, badly, to sing. "Which do you think it is, Dread Lord?"

# 

# Sergeant Crake answers the question by simply turning and letting you look. Along the hall's back wall, his five soldiers stand in a loose but genuine line, mail scrubbed of the worst rust with sand and vinegar borrowed from Marta's kitchen stores, boots blacked, the Undergrowth sprout freshly stitched onto five surcoats that were Wexley flame-orange as recently as yesterday morning. Young Hobb stands at the end of the row with his helmet on the right way round and his chin up, looking like a boy who has been told exactly twice this week that he did something well and intends to be told a third time.

#

That's further than the Wexleys ever got them." He nods once toward the hall's high table, where Clarissa has arranged Tobbin's returned ledgers into neat, damning stacks behind your seat, each one labeled in her own hand. "Records are staged so you look like you already know everything, which you mostly do by now. "Scrubbed mail and a straight row," she says. "Small things. But small things are what the Wexleys never bothered with, and folk notice." She finally drinks, wincing at the cider's bite. "You want my honest read? Half this county's here for free drink, aye. But drink loosens tongues before it loosens legs, and once the talking starts for real, most of them will stay for the same reason Greta and the widow stayed this morning. Nobody's ever asked them a real question before you." She tips her cup slightly toward the hall's noise, the fiddle now joined by two off-key voices. "Ready as you'll get, Dread Lord. County's inside. Question's whether you're ready for eleven villages' worth of grievance, wine, and grain math all landing on you at once."

#
